The letter was received about 3:30 p.m. in Henderson Hall, which Arlington Fire officials described as an administrative building. A gunnery sergeant opened a letter and showed it to a superior, a Pentagon official told NBC News.\n\nUp to 11 people began to feel ill, and the building was evacuated. Three of those people were taken to a hospital in stable condition, officials said in a press release. The marines affected reported itchy hands and face and bloody noses, a marine official said. It is unclear how many people suffered from those symptoms.\n\nA large number of police and medics responded to the Northern Virginia military base, which is near the Pentagon and Arlington National Cemetery. The FBI, Naval Criminal Investigative Service (NCIS) and local hazardous material teams cleared the building with base police.\n\nThe NCIS and FBI are conducting a joint investigation, according to a press release. Information was not available immediately on what the unknown substance could be.\n\n[byline: Shomari Stone, Andrea Swalec and Sophia Barnes]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail rapporteur Mary Marshall\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Wed 28 Feb 2018 8:02 AM ET\nSource: ABC news [edited]\nhttp://abcnews.go.com/US/marines-treated-hazmat-incident-ft-myer-pentagon/story?id=53400402\n\n\nFederal and military officials are investigating a hazmat incident that sickened 11 marines at Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall in Arlington, Virginia, on [Tue 27 Feb 2018]. The FBI and the Naval Criminal Investigative Service were called in when the Marine Corps personnel began feeling ill after an envelope containing an unknown substance was opened at the joint base, which is next to Arlington National Cemetery and near the Pentagon.\n\nPersonnel inside the building were immediately evacuated, officials said, and local fire department hazmat teams responded to the scene within minutes.\n\nA total of 3 marines were transported to a nearby hospital for treatment with non-life threatening conditions. They were treated and released from the hospital late [Tue 27 Feb 2018] night, according to a press release from Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall. The 8 others, who had symptoms ranging from itching to nasal irritation, were being assessed, a marine official told ABC News.\n\nField tests on the suspicious material found inside the envelope came back negative for any known substance, a law enforcement official told ABC News. The envelope and the substance were taken to the FBI's lab at Quantico for further testing. The incident remains under investigation. The FBI and the NCIS are conducting a joint investigation, according to the press release from Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall.\n\nJoint Base Myer-Henderson Hall is the name for the army and marine base commonly-known as Fort Myer, home to the Old Guard honor guard unit and Henderson Hall, where marines are stationed.\n\n[byline: Mark Osborne and Morgan Winsor]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Other reports have indicated there were bloody noses, and burning sensations of the skin. COLI EHEC - AUSTRIA: O146, UNKNOWN SOURCE\n********************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Fri 26 Feb 2021\nSource: Food Safety News [edited]\nhttps://www.foodsafetynews.com/2021/02/investigators-still-looking-for-source-of-outbreak-of-e-coli-infections-in-austria/\n\n\nAustrian authorities are investigating an outbreak of Shiga toxin-producing _E. coli_ [also called enterohemorrhagic _E. coli_ (EHEC)] infections that has affected a handful of people. Between September and December 2020, 6 people fell ill with infections from _E. coli_ O146:H28. Those sick live in 5 federal states. Two people needed hospital treatment. As yet, there is no indication as to the source of the outbreak, according to the Austrian Agency for Health and Food Safety (AGES). It is understood other countries in Europe have not reported related infections.\n\nThe Federal Ministry of Social Affairs, Health, Care and Consumer Protection (BMSGPK) has instructed AGES to investigate the outbreak with the relevant state authorities. Austrian food testing in 2018 found _E. coli_ O146 in 3 samples of fresh game meat and one sample of fermented sausage. In 2017, 4 isolates were typed as _E. coli_ O146 from 2 samples of raw meat from wild ruminants, fresh bovine meat and a fermented sausage.\n\nThe latest Zoonoses Report from the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) and European Centre for Disease Prevention and Control (ECDC) shows _E. coli_ O146 was the 5th most frequent serogroup reported in confirmed human infections in 2018.\n\nAnyone who has developed symptoms of EHEC infection should seek medical attention and tell their doctor about their possible exposure to the bacteria. Specific tests are required to diagnose the infections, which can mimic other illnesses. The symptoms of _E. coli_ infections vary for each person but often include severe stomach cramps and diarrhea, which is often bloody. Most patients recover within 5 to 7 days. Others can develop severe or life-threatening symptoms and complications, according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC).\n\nAbout 5% to 10% of those diagnosed with EHEC infections develop a potentially life-threatening kidney failure complication, known as a hemolytic uremic syndrome (HUS). Symptoms of HUS include fever, abdominal pain, feeling very tired, decreased frequency of urination, small unexplained bruises or bleeding, and pallor.\n\nMany people with HUS recover within a few weeks, but some suffer permanent injuries or death. This condition can occur among people of any age but is most common in children younger than 5 years old because of their immature immune systems, older adults because of deteriorating immune systems, and people with compromised immune systems such as cancer patients. People who experience HUS symptoms should immediately seek emergency medical care. People with HUS will likely be hospitalized because the condition can cause other serious and ongoing problems such as hypertension, chronic kidney disease, brain damage, and neurologic problems.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This Shiga toxin-producing O146 is one of the non-O157 serotypes causing enterohemorrhagic _E. coli_ disease. The source of this zoonotic infection in Austria is not clear at this point. Potential vehicles for transmission include salads, unpasteurized dairy products and undercooked ground beef. - Mod.LL\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nAustria: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/109]", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\n This condition can occur among people of any age but is most common in children younger than 5 years old because of their immature immune systems, older adults because of deteriorating immune systems, and people with compromised immune systems such as cancer patients. \n\nThe latest Zoonoses Report from the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) and European Centre for Disease Prevention and Control (ECDC) shows _E. coli_ O146 was the 5th most frequent serogroup reported in confirmed human infections in 2018. \n\nAbout 5% to 10% of those diagnosed with EHEC infections develop a potentially life-threatening kidney failure complication, known as a hemolytic uremic syndrome (HUS). In 2017, 4 isolates were typed as _E. coli_ O146 from 2 samples of raw meat from wild ruminants, fresh bovine meat and a fermented sausage. Additionally, he had fatigue and pain for many days.\n\nSurgeons later have removed 5 rare intestinal worms with a length of 30-60 centimeters [12-24 in] from the abscesses in his hands.\n\nHead of the hospital's Surgery Ward Dr Tran Thuong Viet said the worm had never been discovered in Viet Nam before but is commonly found in rural areas of Africa with scientific name _Dracunculus medinensis_ -- a species of roundworm that causes Guinea worm disease.\n\nThere is no specific medication [for the disease caused by this worm], doctors have used the usual dose to remove the worms.\n\nThrough investigation, doctors found that the man usually eats living fish and crabs. As the worm is rare in the country, physicians said that it is necessary to study water sources where the man lives because the worm eggs are spread via a water source.\n\n[Byline: Nguyen Quoc; translation: Uyen Phuong]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[It is highly unlikely that this case is due to the Guinea worm _Dracunculus medinensis_. Guinea worm has never be described outside Africa. Transmission is by drinking water contaminated with small copepods or eating raw fish. Recently dogs have been identified as hosts as well (https://www.cdc.gov/dpdx/dracunculiasis/index.html).\n\nIf this is indeed _D. medinensis_, it will be the 1st time the parasite has been reported outside of Africa. With an incubation time of up to 18 months this means contamination in the environment and probably more human cases.\n\nIt is strongly advised that the material removed from the patients is sent for molecular analysis. - Mod.EP\n\nA number of tissue nematodes and larva migrans syndromes, some associated with consuming aquatic animals, can be found in Southeast Asia. Histopathology and DNA analysis of the recovered worms will be key to determining whether this case is a unusual manifestation of a previously reported parasitic nematode, or in fact a novel parasitic infection. - Mod.LXL\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map of Viet Nam: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/66860]\n\n.................................................sb/ep/mj/lxl", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\n As the worm is rare in the country, physicians said that it is necessary to study water sources where the man lives because the worm eggs are spread via a water source. German tabloid Bild reported that an unknown person sprayed an 'irritating substance' at people at the check in desk in Terminal 1.\n\nCops reported that the situation was under control but investigations were underway as the cause was 'still unclear'.\n\nFrankfurt Airport's official Twitter account posted in English: 'Fire department operation completed. No more measured values of tear gas can be detected and the affected area is accessible again.'\n\nFire services were called and the check-in counters were temporarily closed during the incident but have now reopened.\n\nGerman Federal police say that 6 people are being treated for 'light injuries' relating to their airways.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Mon 11 Sep 2017 11:29 BST\nSource: Daily Mail/Mail Online [edited]\nhttp://tinyurl.com/yalwdptd\n\n\nSix people suffered eye irritation and breathing problems after an unknown person sprayed the check-in area of Frankfurt Airport with a mysterious gas on Monday morning [11 Sep 2017]. Firefighters were called to Terminal 1 after several people reported breathing problems at the check-in counters around 11 am.\n\nThe people were treated at the scene and after no trace of gas was detected the counters were reopened, according to The Local.\n\nThe incident was initially reported by Bild as a gas attack, with the paper saying an unknown assailant had sprayed passengers with a mystery substance.\n\nHowever, it now appears that information was incorrect.\n\nAirport authorities say the exact cause of the incident is still unclear, but investigations are ongoing.\n\nThe check-in area was closed for a short time after the scare, before being reopened around 12.30 pm.\n\nNobody was seriously injured during the incident.\n\n[Byline: Chris Pleasance]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This gas could have been any of a number of irritating gases. While substances like ammonia and chlorine may have recognizable smells, other gases may include combustion or industrial gases such as sulfur dioxide, or nitrogen oxides, which may not be quite as recognizable. There are not enough signs and symptoms provided to make much of a supposition as to which gas or gasses may have been involved. - Mod.TG\n\nA HealthMap/ProMED-mail map can be accessed at: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/3697.]\n\n.................................................sb/tg/mj/jh", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\n[1]\n \n\nEmergency services responded to the incident, which occurred inside terminal one at 11 am on Monday morning [11 Sep 2017] local time (7 pm AEST). \n\nThe incident was initially reported by Bild as a gas attack, with the paper saying an unknown assailant had sprayed passengers with a mystery substance. \n\nThe Sun reported someone tear gassed passengers waiting at the check in counter, with breathing difficulties reported among the victims. \n\nThe people were treated at the scene and after no trace of gas was detected the counters were reopened, according to The Local. \n\nFire services were called and the check-in counters were temporarily closed during the incident but have now reopened. Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n< \n\n\nSix people suffered eye irritation and breathing problems after an unknown person sprayed the check-in area of Frankfurt Airport with a mysterious gas on Monday morning Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n< \n\n--\n promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n [Byline: Chris Pleasance]\n\n--\n Firefighters were called to Terminal 1 after several people reported breathing problems at the check-in counters around 11 am.", "reports": [{"diseases": ["unknown", "other"], "syndromes": [], "event_date": ["2021-03-29 00:00:00"], "locations": [{"location": "Germany", "country": "Germany"}, {"location": "Terminal", "country": "unknown"}]}]}, {"archive_id": "5091370", "headline": "PRO/AH/EDR> Drug abuse - USA: (GA) pot. lethal unknown substance, RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=5091370", "date": "2017-06-08 11:08:57", "main_text": "DRUG ABUSE - USA: (GEORGIA) POTENTIALLY LETHAL UNKNOWN SUBSTANCE, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n*****************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Tue 6 Jun 2017\nSource: Georgia Department of Public Health [edited]\nhttps://dph.georgia.gov/press-releases/2017-06-06/hospitalizations-and-deaths-possibly-tied-street-drugs-being-sold-georgia\n\n\nThe Georgia Department of Public Health (DPH) has become aware of a dangerous, potentially lethal substance contained in street drugs surfacing in central and South Georgia. Dozens of patients have been hospitalized and there are reports of deaths that may be associated with the drugs, but confirmation is pending.\n\nThe overdoses have been reported over a 48-hour period in Centerville, Perry, Macon-Warner Robins, and Albany, but the drugs may also be sold on the street in other areas of the state. Patients reportedly purchased yellow pills alleged to be Percocet, an opioid pain medication. The substance has not yet been identified but it is extremely potent and has required massive doses of naloxone (Narcan) to counteract its effects. Testing is being done to identify the pills and the ingredients.\n\n1st responders say patients are unconscious or unresponsive and have difficulty breathing or have stopped breathing. Many patients need to be placed on ventilators. Call 9-1-1 immediately if you have taken the pills or if you think someone has used the drug. Opioid overdose is a very dangerous condition that can result in permanent physical and mental damage or even death if medical treatment is not administered right away.\n\nDPH is working closely with the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, Georgia Poison Center and the Georgia Drugs and Narcotics Agency and federal partners on this investigation.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Purchasing or acquiring drugs from street dealers, even those you think you know, can be a dangerous situation. The drugs may be counterfeits, or mixed with some other substance in an effort to extend the drug, all of which may have unwanted effects, including death.\n\nResults of the testing would be welcome. - Mod.TG]\n\n[As the report suggests that 'massive doses' of nalaxone does work in reversing the effects of this substance, it suggests that the substance may be an opioid class drug with high receptor site uptake. An excellent review article on the use of nalaxone in management of opioid ingestion can be found at: Clarke SF, Dargan PI, Jones AL. Naloxone in opioid poisoning: walking the tightrope. Emerg Med J. 2005 Sep;22(9):612-6, available at: http://emj.bmj.com/content/22/9/612. - Mod.MPP]\n\n[The state of Georgia can be located on the HealthMap/ProMED-mail interactive map at http://healthmap.org/promed/p/213. 'Cameron Elementary School and Hilltop Elementary School have a high percentage of reported cases,' said Shelby Haines, superintendent of schools. The outbreak, though, isn't limited to those 2 schools.\n\n'There are around 50 reported cases,' said Thomas Cook, Marshall County Health Department administrator. State epidemiologists are sending testing kits to the health department for distribution to rapid care facilities, Cook said. Swabs taken from patients will be sent to the West Virginia Bureau of Public Health for testing and diagnosis of the form of infection affecting local residents.\n\nTreating the symptoms is recommended for either form of pneumonia. Antibiotics, however, are prescribed only for bacterial pneumonia. Doctors 'are not going to give antibiotics unless you have a bacteria that you want to eradicate,' Cook explained.\n\nExtensive cleaning is being done in school buildings to prevent additional cases. 'Last week [week of 14 Oct 2019], we began getting phone calls of reported cases of illness in a number of schools,' Haines said. 'When those reports came, we began cleaning with an approved disinfectant to try to get a jump on it. We increased the custodial staff to clean with approved methods. 'The superintendent said the school district has bought its own ionizer, a machine that is being used for cleaning during after-school hours. 'In the evening, we run a cleaning device that sprays disinfectant on all surfaces, on top of regular cleaning. There are some reports in the news of this drug being imported from East Asia (I believe it may have 1st surface in Ohio?). Carfentanil is 10 000 times more potent than morphine (100 times more potent than fentanyl). The DEA also released the following statement regarding a rise in carfentanil overdoses/exposures dating back to Sep 2016: https://www.dea.gov/divisions/hq/2016/hq092216.shtml\n\nIf this ultimately is what ends up being identified in the drug analysis, my best suggestion is to contact the local zoo veterinarian, as these drugs have long been used in zoos by veterinarians and intensive and detailed protocols have been written at all institutions using the drug to help guide those who may need to respond to a potential human exposure. The biggest risk in these exposures is re-narcotization, which might explain why the large doses of naloxone were needed.\nI look forward to hearing the results of the testing; please feel free to email with any questions.\n\n--\nKatherine Fogelberg\nUniversity of Tennessee health sciences center\n<Katherine.Fogelberg@unthsc.edu>\n\n******\n[4]\nDate: Thu 8 Jun 2017\nFrom: Ken Waldrup, DVM\n[email address withheld by request]\n\nIn the northern states, they have been having problems with heroin laced with a carfentanil derivative. The legal carfentanil drug is approximately 700 times more potent than heroin so naloxone has a difficult time reversing such a potent opioid. In dealing with large ungulates immobilized with carfentanil, veterinarians learned that naloxone couldn't cut it 30 years ago. Naltrexone is the reversal agent of choice with veterinary use of carfentanil.\n\n--\nKen Waldrup DVM\n[email withheld on request]\n\n******\n[5]\nDate: Jun 9, 2017 2:33 PM\nFrom: 'Powell, Ryan' <RPowell@rdn.bc.ca>\n\n\nRe: Drug Abuse - USA: (GA) pot. lethal unknown substance, RFI\n\nThe article 'Drug Abuse - USA: (GA) pot. lethal unknown substance, RFI' resonated with me because of the fentanyl crisis occurring in British Columbia, Canada. Contrary to the disease in small ruminants and beef cattle, FMD has been for decades very rare in Israel's dairy cattle. This is mainly due to their robust immunity maintained throughout the years by a compulsory, methodically, State-applied periodical vaccination regime with polyvalent inactivated vaccines that include regionally circulating virus strains.\n\n2. All reported FMD outbreaks, since the establishment of the State of Israel, are considered to have been introduced from the north (Lebanon, Syria) and (less often) east (Jordan). The current outbreak seems to be the 1st one originating in the south-west. FMD was reported from the Gaza strip in 2012 (serotype SAT2) and 2013 (serotype A); in both cases suspected to have been introduced from Egypt. In both events, the virus did not enter Israel's territory.\n\nFor the location of Nir Yitzhak, which is situated in Israel's 'Hadarom' (The South) district, see map at http://tinyurl.com/jd8mmq9.\n\nThe (inactivated, oil emulsion) FMD vaccines applied in Israel for the compulsory vaccination of cattle were composed, in 2015, of the following vaccine strains:\n\n1. 'You're thinking of folks that live in crowded conditions, like dorms. You're thinking of folks with maybe less than optimal eating habits, less than optimal sleep habits. Folks that maybe aren't practicing the best hand hygiene,' Burick said. Those who smoke or have asthma also have an increased risk of contracting the flu or pneumonia. Pneumonia is an infection that can cause fluid buildup in the lungs, and in severe cases can cause breathing difficulties.\n\nAccording to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, there were 184 individuals ages 15 to 24 in the United States who died from influenza and pneumonia in 2015, which is a small fraction of the more than 57 000 people who died from influenza and pneumonia among all ages that year.\n\nAnd MedExpress locations in the area have already seen more pneumonia cases this year [2017] than in all of 2016. Symptoms can sometimes vary with pneumonia, and it can evolve from the flu due to a compromised immune system.\n\n'When you're thinking of the classic symptoms, it's a cough that is persistent, and you're thinking of a fever. Typically a higher fever within that 100-point mark; most folks tend to have that fatigue, that malaise, just not feeling well sensation,' Burick said. 'At the same point, it's not always isolation of symptoms. Some people are also coming in with those flu-like symptoms.'\n\nThe most common form of pneumonia is bacterial, meaning it can be treated with antibiotics. But other forms can be viral or fungal, meaning the illness needs to run its course. The most important thing people should be aware of is prevention techniques, Burick said. 'Practicing great hand hygiene, being cautious not to share food or drinks,' she said. 'It might sound silly, but making sure you're getting adequate sleep and paying attention to your diet.'\n\n[Byline: Kate Malongowski]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The news report above says that there has been 74 percent more cases of young adults with pneumonia between 2015 and 2016 than previously in a 9-county region that includes Beaver County in the US state of Pennsylvania, but fails to indicate what these counties are or to give the microbial causes for this increase.\n\nCenter Township, a suburban community approximately 25 mi (40 km) northwest of Pittsburgh, is located in Beaver County, Pennsylvania, United States (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_Township,_Beaver_County,_Pennsylvania). Beaver County is on the border with the states of West Virginia and Ohio (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaver_County,_Pennsylvania#Adjacent_counties) and is part of the Pittsburgh, PA Metropolitan Statistical Area. Adjacent counties are Lawrence (north), Butler (east), Allegheny (southeast), Washington (south), Hancock, West Virginia (west) and Columbiana, Ohio (west).\n\nCommunity-acquired pneumonia (CAP) can be caused by a variety of microorganisms, including bacteria, viruses, and, less commonly, fungi. Common bacterial causes of CAP in the United States are _Streptococcus pneumoniae_ (also called pneumococcus), _Legionella pneumophila_, _Staphylococcus aureus_, _Mycoplasma pneumoniae_, and _Chlamydia pnueumoniae_. Outbreaks of CAP caused by M. pneumoniae occur mostly in crowded environments, like households, schools, college dormitories, and military barracks, when coughing releases small droplets of respiratory secretions into the air that are inhaled by close contacts. The opioid epidemic in the U.S. could also be causing an increase in cases of CAP as a result of aspiration of anaerobic bacterial mouth flora or as a result of injection drug use giving rise to hematogenous _Staphylococcus aureus_ pneumonia.\n\nViruses, such as influenza, also can cause of outbreaks of CAP. Travel-associated pneumonia may be caused by Middle East respiratory syndrome coronavirus (MERS-CoV) indigenous to the Arabian Peninsula or H5N1 or H7N9 strains of avian influenza indigenous to Asia. Republic of Korea\n------------------------------------------------------\nOn 29 Oct 2015, the National IHR Focal Point of the Republic of Korea notified WHO of a cluster of cases with respiratory symptoms in Seoul. Between [19 and 29 Oct 2015], 3 people who work in the same facility developed symptoms of pneumonia. From [22 to 24 Oct 2015], they were admitted to hospital. On [27 Oct 2015], the hospital isolated the patients and alerted local health authorities, which then informed the Korean Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (KCDC).\n\nAdditional information on the outbreak\n-------------------------------------------\nTo date, 84 cases with respiratory symptoms have been identified; 55 of them were diagnosed with pneumonia and 29 cases were mildly symptomatic. The 55 patients with pneumonia were isolated in 7 different hospitals while the 29 patients with mild symptoms were under home quarantine.\n\nAs of [11 Nov 2015], only 1 of the 55 patients with pneumonia was still hospitalized; the other 54 cases had all been discharged. Currently, none of the patients is in critical condition.\n\nPublic health response\n----------------------\nIn response to the outbreak, KCDC and the government of the Republic of Korea have implemented a series of public health measures: issued daily press releases to the public; conducted contact tracing -- 1664 contacts have been monitored on a daily basis; established a hotline for reporting potentially-linked cases; requested hospitals to report pneumonia cases with potential links to the cluster; closed and disinfected the affected facility.\n\nSo far, all PCR tests carried out by the KCDC have been negative, including for adenovirus, respiratory syncytial virus, parainfluenza virus, metapneumovirus, bocavirus, influenza virus, and coronavirus (including MERS-CoV), as well as for _Mycoplasma_, _Chlamydia_, _Corynebacterium_, __Bordetella_, Brucella_, _Coxiella_, and _Legionella_.\n\nAt present, there is no evidence of human-to-human transmission. Investigation on the cause of the outbreak is ongoing.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[So far no etiologic agent has been identified, but we still wait for a full epidemiologic description of the outbreak at Konkuk University School of Veterinary Sciences, which has now involved a total of 84 individuals with respiratory symptoms, 55 of whom had pneumonia and 29 were mildly symptomatic, presumably without pneumonia. - Mod.ML\n\nA HealthMap/ProMED-mail map can be accessed at: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/46552.]", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\n In response to the outbreak, KCDC and the government of the Republic of Korea have implemented a series of public health measures: issued daily press releases to the public; conducted contact tracing -- 1664 contacts have been monitored on a daily basis; established a hotline for reporting potentially-linked cases; requested hospitals to report pneumonia cases with potential links to the cluster; closed and disinfected the affected facility. It is estimated that the disease has low severity since its progression is relatively slow.\n* 2 out of 50 suspected patients who did not show symptoms of a fever initially:\nCase 1: (initial) headache, muscle aches, chills, (currently) no fever, improvement in symptoms, improvement in pneumonia findings.\nCase 2: (initial) cough, headache, (currently) no fever, but the presence of symptoms and pneumonia findings\nFor the abnormalities found in some lung CT scans, lung tissues are collected for testing.\nPathogen test: There is 90 per cent progress on genetic and antibody testing for the 7 kinds of bacteria and 9 kinds of virus of all the suspected patients. Brucellosis, Q fever, legionellosis shall be reassayed through secondary antibody inspection after 3 weeks.\nIn addition, the test for fungal culture is in progress for 30 suspected patients using the remaining samples after bacteria and virus scan. This may take a few days to few months, and it usually takes 2 to 4 weeks of observation.\nEnvironmental studies: environmental samples were collected from inside the building, which is currently under investigation (started 28 Oct 2015), and it will take about 2 weeks.\nOn the other hand, another 192 students from other departments who entered the building are currently monitored by the KCDC Call Center (109) (a total of 1664).\n* Number of people who are subjected to be monitored: (30 Oct 2015) 964; (31 Oct 2015) 1472; (1 Nov 15) 1664\n87 individuals who are living with the 50 suspected patients are being monitored by public health center for unusual symptoms.\nSo far, unusual cases are not confirmed from the result of monitoring.\n* The system to encourage 527 applicants of the SK Group employment exam to report to the KCDC Call Center (109) is retained.\nKCDC are investigating and taking necessary steps to find the cause and manage the respiratory disease.\nKCDC will actively cooperate with relevant ministries and academic-medical specialists, and will plan to inform the public and the media often.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The translations were requested of colleagues in Seoul by ProMED-mail consultant, Daniel Lucey, MD of Georgetown University and Jayoung Park. ProMED-mail would like to thank volunteer Korean subscribers for assisting with translations of the daily South Korean MOH reports.\n\nAs of today (2 Nov 2015), the latest tally of cases of an acute febrile illness with chest x-ray findings of pneumonia at Konkuk University is 50. All cases have been hospitalized in isolation, but all apparently have mild illness. 96 per cent had fever (temperature above 37.5 C) (99 F), but we are not told the height of the fever. Only 32 per cent had a cough, and only 14 per cent had a cough productive of sputum. We are not told if any had difficulty breathing. Though we are told 8 per cent had 'chest aches', we are not told if the chest pain was pleuritic in nature.\n\nThe 1st reports of the outbreak at Konkuk University said only graduate students in the veterinary school were affected, but now the affected individuals are only characterized as 'workers' in the university's Animal Life Sciences Building; however, we are not told the nature of their work. The outbreak has involved workers on the 3rd-7th floors, but the attack rates were usually highest among workers on the 5th and 7th floors.\n\nThere are an additional 26 cases who were in the Konkuk University Animal Life Sciences Building after 8 Oct 2015 with fever, but apparently failed to have radiographic evidence of pneumonia. There has been no evidence of secondary spread among contacts of the patients.\n\nThe 1st case became symptomatic on 19 Oct 2015, and the outbreak intensified between 25 and 27 Oct 2015 (29 cases, 58 per cent of total cases). The Animal Life Sciences building was closed on 28 Oct 2015 and there have been no new cases in the past 2 days. So far, no etiologic agent has been identified. Unusual findings have not been confirmed until now.\n\nTest results:\n- For the cause, genetic testing and serum antibody tests were conducted on some patients, which were confirmed negative.\n- PCR test result negative infectious disease\n- respiratory bacteria: mycoplasma, chlamydia, whooping cough, diphtheria\n- respiratory viruses: Merck's, adenovirus, RS virus, parainfluenza virus, virus meth pneumophila, Boca virus, influenza virus, coronavirus\n- PCR negative [for?] infectious diseases in antibody test progress\nBrucellosis, Q fever, Legionella (3 weeks after retesting with convalescent serum)\n*Although test came out negative, it is not excluded from the cause of infection, and retest will be conducted according to symptoms.\n- Chemical materials and environmental factors, as well as a mass outbreak by infectious pathogens will be investigated from various angles.\n\nMeanwhile, Konkuk University Animal Life Science building was closed down on 28 Oct 2015. People who visited the building from 8-28 Oct 2015 and have fever are encourged to report to the KCDC Call Center (109).\nAlso, the SK Group held an employment exam at the building on 25 Oct 2015. Health authorities have placed all 21 in quarantine and closed off the school building. The Korea Centers for Disease Control and Prevention [KCDC] on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015] said the victims started coming down with pneumonia last week, and a team of epidemiologists have been dispatched to the university.\n\nAccording to the KCDC, those infected are master's and doctoral candidates who used the school's lab from [19 to 28 Oct 2015]. They are being treated in isolation at state-run hospitals.\n\nThe 1st 4 graduate students who showed symptoms were hospitalized at Konkuk University Medical Center and then transferred to the National Medical Center on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015]. All of them visited a cattle fair in Gyeonggi Province last week as well as an animal farm owned by the university in Chungju, North Chungcheong Province.\n\nA university official said they may have contracted brucellosis, which infects cattle and can be transmitted to humans. But some experts suspect Q fever, caused by the _Coxiella burnetii_ bacteria found in the droppings of cattle, swine and sheep. It causes airborne infections among humans. Symptoms such as fever, headache and muscle aches appear after a 2-week gestation period. But Song Dae-sup at Korea University said, 'Brucellosis and Q fever are not commonly found in Korea and are rarely passed on to humans. We need to look at the possibility of pneumonia caused by germs or other toxic agents.'\n\nLee Jae-gap at Hallym University Medical Center said since only the 4 visited the animal farm, the infection could be mycoplasma pneumonia or whooping cough, which sometimes occur in schools or communities.\n\nKonkuk University sealed off the veterinary school building and told the school's 850 staff and students to report any suspicious symptoms. The building was thoroughly disinfected on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015] morning as well, according to school officials.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This news report was also submitted by Dan Silver, ProMED-mail Rapporteur.]\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Fri 30 Oct 2015\nSource: The Chosun Ilbo [edited]\nhttp://english.chosun.com/site/data/html_dir/2015/10/30/2015103001031.html\n\n\n10 more graduate students have come down with a mysterious pneumonia attack at Konkuk University's Seoul campus on Thursday [29 Oct 2015], bringing the total to 31.\n\n21 people were diagnosed with the same symptoms earlier. But all have so far tested negative for a dozen well-known infectious diseases.\n\n'We're still trying to figure out the cause,' a spokesman for the Korea Centers for Disease Control and Prevention [KCDC] said Thursday.\n\nStudents look at instructions in front of a makeshift clinic at Konkuk University in Seoul on Thursday [29 Oct 2015]. The school said all patients are graduate students at the school of veterinary science and most have mild symptoms.\n\n23 are in isolation at state-run hospitals, while 8 with very mild symptoms are quarantined at home. All have tested negative for brucellosis, Q fever, and _Legionella_, which were among the prime suspects of the mysterious infection. They also tested negative for bacterial diseases like _Mycoplasma_ and _Chlamydia_ and viruses like Middle East respiratory syndrome [MERS] and flu.\n\nMeanwhile, it has emerged that the SK Group conducted recruitment exams on the campus last Sunday [25 Oct 2015], when the outbreak was probably already underway. Authorities asked 500 people who took the exams to report to the KCDC if they have symptoms like high fever.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This news report was also submitted by Dan Silver, ProMED-mail Rapporteur.]\n\n[The fact that a large group of veterinary graduate students became ill with pneumonia over a short period of time suggests a point source outbreak, i.e., they were all exposed to the same source over a brief time. The development of additional cases over time and geographic areas will be very useful in determining whether the cases are related to a point source.\n\nWe are not told exactly the severity of the illness, but almost 75 percent of cases were ill enough to require hospitalization. The fact that the illness seems at the present time to be limited to graduate veterinary students suggests a zoonosis. Brucellosis, Q fever, MERS, and influenza, as well as legionellosis, chlamydiosis, and _Mycoplasma_ infection were said to have been ruled out, but the report does not mention SARS. I don't know how legionellosis was ruled out, but Pontiac fever, a non-pneumonic form of legionellosis, occurs as a point source outbreak with high attack rates following exposure to aerosolized _Legionella_. Pontiac fever is diagnosed serologically; culture and legionella urinary antigen are usually negative. However, the severity of the Pontiac fever is so mild that it usually does require hospitalization. Other etiologies to be considered should include psittacosis (again I am unsure how a chlamydial infection was ruled out), tularemia, pneumonic plague, and anthrax. Histoplasmosis, although very rare in South Korea, can also cause a point source outbreak of an acute respiratory illness. More information is obviously needed from knowledgeable sources to develop a list of potential etiologies.\n\nKonkuk University is a private university located in Seoul and Chungju. Gyeonggi Province surrounds Seoul. Chungju is a city in North Chungcheong Province, which is southeast of Seoul. It confirmed that the case was in a US citizen born outside the Americas and indicated that the patient's exposure to the BSE/vCJD agent most likely occurred before he moved to the United States; the patient had resided in Kuwait, Russia and Lebanon.\n\nThe completed investigation did not support the patient's having had extended travel to European countries, including the United Kingdom, or travel to Saudi Arabia. The specific overseas country where this patient's infection [could have] occurred is less clear, largely because the investigation did not definitely link him to a country where other known vCJD cases likely had been infected.\n\nVariant Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease (vCJD), 1st described in 1996 in the United Kingdom, is a rare, degenerative, fatal brain disorder in humans. It is believed to be caused by consumption of products from cows with the disease bovine spongiform encephalopathy (BSE, or 'mad cow' disease). Worldwide, more than 220 variant CJD patients have been reported, with a majority of them in the United Kingdom (177 cases) and France (27 cases).\n\nThis case is the 4th to be reported in the United States. In each of the 3 previous cases, infection likely occurred outside the United States, including the United Kingdom (2 cases) and Saudi Arabia (1 case). The history of this 4th patient, including extensive travel to Europe and the Middle East, supports the likelihood that infection occurred outside the United States. CDC assisted the Texas Department of State Health Services' (DSHS) investigation of this case and has continued to establish the patient's history, including the potential source of infection.\n\nThe classic form of CJD, which is not caused by the BSE agent, occurs worldwide, including in the United States. Annually, for every one million people in the United States, 1-2 develop classic CJD.\n\nMore information about variant CJD, including how it differs from classic CJD, is available in the Variant Creutzfeldt-Jakob Disease Fact Sheet (http://www.cdc.gov/ncidod/dvrd/vcjd/factsheet_nvcjd.htm).\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nTerry S. It also led to the death of tens of million poultry, OIE said. Although a pandemic was averted, the H5N1 strain is still present. agalactia in sheep, Lorraine (France): request for information from other regions\n------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nA number of sheep flocks in Lorraine [map at http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lorraine_in_France.svgare] are currently facing a severe episode of significant reduction or a total absence of lactation in ewes. The Departments of Meurthe-et-Moselle and Moselle seem particularly concerned. 'The GDS [National Federation of Animal Health Protection Groups] and veterinary practitioners have developed a framework for investigations in cooperation with Prof Schelcher, Veterinary School, Toulouse.\n\nThe phenomenon has been observed since the beginning of the lambing season. On 14 Dec 2012, GDS Meurthe-et-Moselle identified agalactia in 15 out of a total of about 200 farms. Affected farms were visited, the attack rate of the lambing ewes was recorded as 50 to 100 percent. The reported cases appear scattered in the departments concerned, demonstrating absence of colostrum/milk during the 1st post-parturition days. This leads to the need to hand-feed the lambs. Lactation appears again (with or without therapeutic treatment) in the ewes 2-8 days post parturition.\n\nNo particular clinical symptoms have been seen in the ewes prior to the observed compromised lactation.\n\nThe established platform of investigation applies to veterinarians and farmers in other geographical regions to report similar observations to a given e-mail address (see source url).\n\n[Byline: Michel Jeanney]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This is not a case of the infectious mycoplasma disease in sheep and goats called 'contagious agalactiae', which, on top of its effect upon lactation, also causes ocular and joints (arthritic) changes.\n\nUpdated results of the surveillance and of the epidemiological investigation are anticipated with interest. According to this report, the Israeli, who recently arrived in China after travelling [in] India, contacted an Israeli businessman a few days ago and told him he was feeling ill, was suffering from severe back pain, had difficulty drinking and was vomiting constantly.\n\nThe businessman rushed the Israeli to a local hospital where he underwent a cardiac catheterization procedure. While at the hospital the Israeli suffered from hallucinations during which he claimed the Chinese doctors were trying to harvest his organs.\n\nThe physicians initially thought the man was suffering from some sort of mental illness and tried to determine whether he used drugs. Some doctors suggested transferring the Israeli to a psychiatric hospital after he recuperated, but his condition quickly deteriorated. He slipped in and out of consciousness, and the doctors hooked him up to a ventilator.\n\nThe mystery was solved when an infectious disease specialist was rushed to the Israeli's room and determined that he had contracted rabies. It remains unclear whether the Israeli, who died on Wed 19 Sep 2012, [had been] bitten by a dog and if so when [and where].\n\nMore than 55 000 people dies of rabies each year, [many] in India.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[People contract rabies predominantly following a deep bite or scratch by an infected animal. Dogs are the main host and transmitter of rabies in Asia. The initial symptoms of rabies are fever and often pain or an unusual or unexplained tingling, pricking or burning sensation (paraesthesia) at the wound site. As the virus spreads through the central nervous system, progressive, fatal inflammation of the brain and spinal cord develops. 2 forms of the disease can follow. People with furious rabies exhibit signs of hyperactivity, excited behaviour, hydrophobia and sometimes aerophobia. After a few days, death occurs by cardio-respiratory arrest. Paralytic rabies accounts for about 30 percent of the total number of human cases.\n\nNo tests are available to diagnose rabies infection in humans before the onset of clinical disease, and unless the rabies-specific signs of hydrophobia or aerophobia are present, the clinical diagnosis may be difficult. Human rabies can be confirmed intra-vitam and post mortem by various diagnostic techniques aimed at detecting whole virus, viral antigens or nucleic acids in infected tissues (brain, skin, urine or saliva). [See: http://www.who.int/mediacentre/factsheets/fs099/en/index.html].\n\nThe preceding press report does not identify the type of test used to establish the diagnosis. The incubation period for rabies virus infection in humans is typically 1-3 months, but may range from less than one week to more than one year, depending among other things on on the site and size of the initial wound. The report lacks information on the date of arrival of the patient in Beijing or the length of his stay India [or elsewhere]. The ship owners have to provide\nspecial protective outerwear and respiratory equipment for\nanti-rodent treatment. - Corr.VM\n\nPhosphine gas is frequently used in the grain industry for fumigating\ngrain, especially grains that are held for any period of time. The\nfumigation decreases weevils and rodents preying on the grain.\n\nPhosphine gas is a colorless, inflammable gas with carbide or\nfish-like odor and some describe it as a garlic-like odor. It is most\nfrequently toxic by inhalation. The amount that is toxic is relative\nto the species inhaling it. The amount per cubic meter and the length\nof time of exposure govern the toxicity. The higher the amount means\nthe lower the time necessary to cause toxicity and conversely, the\nlower the amount per cubic meter the longer the time of exposure\nrequired to produce intoxication. The levels are not cumulative.\n\nPhosphine is most often sold in the form of aluminium phosphide,\ncalcium phosphide, or zinc phosphide pellets. Phosphine is released\nwhen it encounters moisture, such as atmospheric moisture or gastric\nacid in the stomach of rodents.\n\nIf the crew believed there were fish on board then they may not have\nthought a fishy odor to be odd. However, with the grain off-gassing\nin the ship's hold and no outside ventilation for the crew, this was\na set up for a deadly situation.\n\nPhosphine is a very toxic gas, and is also generated as a by-product\nduring the manufacturing of methamphetamine. - Mod.TG]", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Thu 20 Mar 2008\n The higher the amount means\nthe lower the time necessary to cause toxicity and conversely, the\nlower the amount per cubic meter the longer the time of exposure\nrequired to produce intoxication. China (03)", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=37850", "date": "2007-11-18 18:00:12", "main_text": "UNKNOWN ILLNESS, GIANT PANDAS - CHINA (03)\n******************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Fri 16 Nov 2007\nSource: China Daily [edited]\n<http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/china/2007-11/16/content_6259208.htm>\n\n\nThis year's [2007] outbreak of contagious diseases among giant pandas\nhas emphasized the need for more measures to ensure the bears' future\nsafety, delegates to the 18th Annual Conference of the Chinese\nCommittee of Breeding Techniques for the Giant Panda have said.\n\nZhang Zhihe, the committee's chairman, said to avoid possible future\noutbreaks of highly infectious diseases, such as SARS (severe acute\nrespiratory syndrome) and bird flu, it is critical to do more\nresearch on the supervision, prevention and treatment of such\nconditions -- as well as so far undiagnosed diseases -- and establish\nan emergency response system.\n\nGiant pandas have been forced to move from a mountainous area of\nsouthwestern China due to food shortages, as their bamboo food\nflowers and dies as part of a natural cycle, an animal expert said.\n\nSpeaking at the 5-day conference, which ended Thursday [15 Nov 2007]\nin the Sichuan provincial capital, Yang Xuyu, deputy chief of Sichuan\nWildlife Management Station, said about 20 panda cubs are bred in\ncaptivity every year in China. But if the bears live together in\nconfined spaces, contagious diseases can quickly spread.\n\nA delegate who asked not to be named said 10 pandas at the Wolong\nNature Reserve this year [2007] became infected with a rare\ncontagious disease from which 2 of them later died [Could the nature\nof the suspected 'rare' disease be specified? Clinical signs,\nlaboratory tests etc. will be helpful. - Mod.AS].\n\nVets from the Chengdu Research Base of Giant Panda Breeding, where\nZhang is based, worked with staff from Wolong to treat the sick\npandas but failed to diagnose the ailment, he said.\n\nYang said that in an effort to prevent the spread of potentially\nfatal diseases, additional enclosures for the bears will be built at\nboth Chengdu and Wolong.\n\nThe State Forestry Administration recently gave Wolong 20 million\nyuan [USD 2.7 million] to build 40 new dens some 20 km from its\nexisting ones. The Chengdu base is currently considering possible\nsites for its new compounds, he said.\n\nYang also warned of the danger of bamboo flowering, which, since\n2005, has expanded to an area of 24 000 hectares in Sichuan, about\n1.4 percent of the edible bamboo in the province, he told China Daily.\n\nNine varieties of bamboo have been seen flowering, which account for\nabout 30 percent of the varieties eaten by pandas.\n\nIn the 1980s, in the mountainous regions of Sichuan, extensive\nblossoming of the arrow bamboo -- the pandas' favorite -- led to many\nbears dying of disease and starvation, Yang said.\n\nThis year [2007], to avoid a recurrence, the Sichuan provincial\nforestry bureau has developed an emergency response plan and asked\nlocal forestry bureaus to implement it in the event of extensive\nblossoming.\n\nYang said that if 15 percent of the total bamboo area or 100 percent\nof a single variety is found to be flowering, all bears in that area\nwill be inoculated and/or relocated to ensure their safety.\n\nOften referred to as living fossils, giant pandas are found mainly in\nSichuan, which is home to about 1200 of them, or 76 percent of the\ncountry's total.\n\nMore than 80 officials and experts from animal protection\norganizations in 8 countries attended this year's [2007] conference.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Rapporteur Dan Silver\n\n[For Bill Karesh's commentary, see 20071114.3691. - Mod.AS]", "summary": "\n\nZhang Zhihe, the committee's chairman, said to avoid possible future\noutbreaks of highly infectious diseases, such as SARS (severe acute\nrespiratory syndrome) and bird flu, it is critical to do more\nresearch on the supervision, prevention and treatment of such\nconditions -- as well as so far undiagnosed diseases -- and establish\nan emergency response system. Despite a great deal\nof research on the physiology, reproductive biology, and diet of\npandas in the wild and in captivity, there is little information on\nwild panda mortality. Here, we integrate previously unavailable data\non mortality of wild pandas. We report 3 recent phases of panda\nmortality: deaths due to bamboo flowering in the 1970s and 1980s;\nsurprisingly extensive poaching in the 1980s and 1990s; and the\ngrowing importance of a parasitic infection over the past few years.\nOur analyses suggest that the current most significant threat to wild\npanda survival is disease due to extra-intestinal migration (visceral\nlarva migrans) of an ascarid nematode. We demonstrate that the\nprobability of death of wild pandas being caused by this disease\nincreased significantly between 1971 and 2006 and discuss the\npossible factors leading to the emergence of this disease.\n\n[Jin-Shuo Zhang (1,2), Peter Daszak (3), Hua-Li Huang (4), Guang-You\nYang (5), A. Marm Kilpatrick (3), and Shu-Yi Zhang (2)\n\n1. Institute of Zoology and Graduate University, Chinese Academy of\nSciences, Beijing, 100080, China\n2. A ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Wed 28 Nov 2007\n Communicated by:\nDr Peter Daszak\nExecutive Director,\nConsortium for Conservation Medicine,\nNew York, NY 10001\n Co-chair, IUCN Species Survival Commission - Wildlife Health Specialist\nGroup\nDirector, Field Veterinary Program\nWildlife Conservation Society\n2300 Southern Blvd. Despite a great deal\nof research on the physiology, reproductive biology, and diet of\npandas in the wild and in captivity, there is little information on\nwild panda mortality. We report 3 recent phases of panda\nmortality: deaths due to bamboo flowering in the 1970s and 1980s;\nsurprisingly extensive poaching in the 1980s and 1990s; and the\ngrowing importance of a parasitic infection over the past few years. We demonstrate that the\nprobability of death of wild pandas being caused by this disease\nincreased significantly between 1971 and 2006 and discuss the\npossible factors leading to the emergence of this disease. Rappt.DS, edited]\n<http://news.sina.com.cn/o/2007-11-12/114512888303s.shtml>\n\n\nAt the opening of the 18th Annual Conference of the Chinese Committee\nof Breeding Techniques for Giant Pandas in Chengdu, Sichuan,\nresearcher Zhihe Zhang, director of the Committee, presented this\nyear's [2007] Committee work report to the conference.\n\nIt was stated at the conference that there has been an outbreak of an\nunknown infectious disease among pandas in some nature reserves and\nprotective units in China this year [2007]. The health and safety of\nthe captive and wild giant panda species has therefore become a key\nissue at this year's conference.\n\n'Small scale outbreak[s] of disease this year [2007] in China alert\nus to the need to pay active attention to the safety of the [giant\npanda] population.' Zhihe Zhang stated that population safety is one\nof the most important issues affecting the survival of the giant\npanda. To avoid the emergence of vicious infectious diseases similar\nto SARS [severe acute respiratory syndrome] or avian influenza in the\ngiant panda population, it is extremely important to immediately\nstrengthen monitoring, prevention, and treatment/research of canine\ndistemper virus and other known and unknown infectious diseases. It\nis also extremely urgent to organize response teams, equipment, and\nemergency systems.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Rapporteur Dan Silver\n\n[ProMED-mail has heard little regarding disease in giant pandas and\nhas referred this story to William Karesh of the Wildlife\nConservation Society for further comment. - Ed.LM]\n\n[Unfortunately, the news report provides little for interpretation.\nIf indeed the problems being mentioned are due to an infectious\ndisease, there are quite a few that have been reported over the years\nthat can infect giant pandas. Serological evidence of exposure to\ncanine viruses such as morbillivirus, adenovirus, parvovirus, and\ncoronavirus has been reported. Of course, test validation for pandas\nis unlikely and the possibility of cross-reaction to related viruses\nis quite possible. Bacterial septicemias due to _E. coli_ have been\nreported in captive pandas also.\n\nGiven the behavioral ecology (mostly solitary animals except during\nan extremely brief breeding season and living at low densities)\ncontact rates among wild pandas would be very low. Though not\nimpossible, it would seem unlikely that that same infectious agent\nwas spreading among pandas unless it had an extremely long incubation\nand/or period of shedding and not rapidly fatal. More likely is that\nthey are being exposed to organisms from other species, including\ndomestic animals that may be contaminating the limited remaining\npanda habitat, which may lead to cross-species transmission of the\nagents. Non-infectious causes such as environmental contaminants\nshould not be completely discounted either.\n\nPossibly, the more valuable piece of information in this news report\nis the official recognition for the need for better surveillance and\nresponse teams to investigate morbidity and mortality. If coordinated\nwith local domestic animal health monitoring or reporting systems\naround protected areas, it may shed light on prevalence of a number\nof diseases and sources of infection.\n\nWilliam B. COLI O157, UNKNOWN SOURCE - AUSTRALIA (SOUTH AUSTRALIA)\n**********************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: Tue 13 Feb 2007\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: Adelaide Now [edited]\n<http://www.news.com.au/adelaidenow/story/0,22606,21222831-5006301,00.html>\n\nThe source of a spate of _E. coli_ [O157] infections across South\nAustralia (SA) remains a mystery as authorities yesterday, 12 Feb\n2007, admitted they were not confident of finding the cause.\nPublic health director Dr. Kevin Buckett said finding the origin of\nthe potentially fatal bacteria was proving to be an uphill battle.\n'We're not overly confident but we're working very hard to track it\n(the cause) down,' Dr. Buckett said. 'We'll keep pursuing it as far\nas we can.'\nThe admission came as the Health Department confirmed 3 new cases of\n_E. coli_ infection. There have now been 10 cases reported in 2007,\nwhich is more than a quarter of the average yearly total.\n'Here in SA, we get around 30 to 40 cases of all strains of _E. coli_\neach year,' he said. 'These cases are usually quite sporadic and\noccur throughout the year. 'When we get a lot of cases occurring at\nonce and they seem to be linked in some way, then I guess we call\nthis an outbreak,' Dr. Buckett said.\nHe said the fact that the infected people lived in different areas --\nincluding one in regional SA -- and were aged between 2 and 81 years\nof age, made identifying common links difficult.\nFlinders University gastroenterologist Professor Graeme Young said\nfinding the cause of the outbreak would involve a degree of\n'detective work'. 'I think that if there isn't a common factor\nbetween the people, it makes it very hard to understand why this is\nhappening,' Professor Young said.\n[Byline: Jessica Leo]\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n [Byline: Jessica Leo]\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org> He said the fact that the infected people lived in different areas --\nincluding one in regional SA -- and were aged between 2 and 81 years\nof age, made identifying common links difficult. "PRO/AH/EDR> Unknown illness, fatal, lions - India: RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=2793", "date": "2006-09-20 00:00:00", "main_text": "UNKNOWN ILLNESS, FATAL, LIONS - INDIA: REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n*************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: 20 Sep 2006\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: AP via NY Times [edited]\n<http://www.nytimes.com/aponline/world/AP-India-Dying-Lions.html?_r=1&oref=slogin>\n\nMystery Disease Killing Lions in India\n-------------------------------------------\nNearly 2 dozen crossbred lions are slowly dying in northern India\nfrom a mysterious disease afflicting the hybrid offspring of Asiatic\nand African cats paired in a discontinued experimental program.\nZookeepers are mournfully watching the results of the program, which\nbegan in the late 1980s at the Chhatbir Zoo and was ended in 2002,\nafter many of the nearly 80 crossbred lions were struck by a\nmysterious disease linked to inbreeding and a weakened gene pool,\nsaid Kuldip Kumar, Punjab state's conservator of forests and wildlife.\nWildlife officials had originally hoped the hybrid cats could be\nintroduced into the wild in an effort to bolster India's endangered\nwild lion population.\nWhen the program ended, all of the male lions were given vasectomies\nto prevent further breeding, Kumar said.\nIndian wildlife laws prohibit killing the animals.\nIt will take about 6 years for the remaining 22 crossbred lions to\ndie of natural causes, Kumar said.\nZoo authorities have decided to COLI O157 - USA (MULTISTATE): UNKNOWN SOURCE\n***********************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: Fri 7 Apr 2006\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: FoodConsumer.org [edited]\n<http://www.foodconsumer.org/777/8/FSIS_Reminds_Consumers_to_Properly_Handle_and_Cook_Ground_Beef_Products_.shtml>\n\nFSIS: Handle ground beef products properly\n-----------------------------------------------\nThe USA Department of Agriculture's Food Safety and Inspection\nService (FSIS) is issuing a public health alert to remind consumers\nto ensure that meat products are fully cooked and properly handled\nbefore they are consumed.\nFSIS has received reports of 14 illnesses caused by _E. coli_ O157:H7\nwith matching microbiological profiles. There is no link to a\nspecific product, but illnesses from this pathogen can be associated\nwith consumption of raw or undercooked ground beef. Illnesses have\nbeen found in California, Iowa, New York, Ohio, Michigan, Rhode\nIsland and Wisconsin. These illnesses occurred over a 6-month period,\nbeginning in September 2005 through March 2006, and FSIS is working\nclosely with State and local health officials to determine the\nexposure that led to illness.\nTherefore, FSIS wants to remind all consumers of the proper handling\nand cooking of meat products. Safe steps in food handling, cooking,\nand storage are essential to prevent foodborne illness. Consumers\nshould follow the 4 guidelines to keep food safe:\n1. Clean: Wash hands and surfaces often. Wash your hands with warm,\nsoapy water for 20 seconds before and after handling food. Wash your\ncutting boards, dishes, etc. with hot, soapy water after preparing\neach food item. Wash fruits and vegetables with cold water before\nusing. There is no need to wash or rinse meat or poultry.\n2. Separate: Don't cross-contaminate. Separate raw, cooked, and\nready-to-eat foods while shopping, preparing, or storing. Never place\ncooked food on a plate which previously held raw meat, poultry, or\nseafood.\n3. Cook: Cook food to proper temperatures. To be sure bacteria and\npathogens are destroyed, cook ground beef products to 160 F. Use a\nfood thermometer to be sure!\n4. Chill: Refrigerate promptly. Refrigerate or freeze perishables,\nprepared foods, and leftovers within 2 hours or sooner.\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[Matching microbiological profiles (presumably genetic matches)\noccurring over 6 months and scattered across the USA suggest a common\nreservoir that is nonperishable, such as frozen ground beef rather\nthan unpasteurized milk or produce. Many Immokalee growers may be forced out of\nbusiness.\nAccording to Roberts, some affected fields are losing 100 per cent of their\nproduction. With few clues to go on, scientists say it's very likely this\nsituation will get worse.\nConsumers can identify an infected melon by examining the rind. Torres <torresj@email.com>\nSource: El Universal, Venezuela [trans. J. Gonzalez, J. Torres; edited]\n<http://noticias.eluniversal.com/2004/10/05/ccs_art_05282A.shtml>\n\nPolice officers in the Venezuelan State of Miranda are continuing to\nenforce an order prohibiting use of all beaches in the Higuerote\narea, after 468 people were sickened during the past weekend through\n[presumed] contamination of the Barlovento coast.\nPolicemen have been stationed on the roads accessing Caracolito,\nChirimena, Los Totumos, Buche, Puerto Frances, and other beaches\nlocated in the Higuerote area, in order to prevent tourists and\nresidents from developing the symptoms others reported last weekend.\nThe same symptoms were reported in the same area in 1996 and 1998.\nPhysicians at the Higuerote and Caucagua central hospitals cared for\npatients presenting with nausea, vomiting, itching, and general\nrespiratory symptoms. 6 of the people affected had to be sent to a\nclinic in the capital in order to obtain proper medical care.\nMiranda Fire Chief Jose Antonio Plascencia announced that special\npersonnel have been sent to the area to care for the affected persons\nand that the majority of the victims were treated on an outpatient\nbasis. He explained that even though both physicians and paramedics\nassume that the condition has an environmental origin, all affected\npersons claim to have allergic and respiratory symptoms. He recalled\nthat some time ago the same phenomenon occurred in this area, but the\nauthorities could not determine its origin. The Fire Chief stated\nthat no one will be allowed on the beaches in the next 48 hours.\nA decree by the State Governor prohibited the use of the affected\nareas in order to prevent a recurrence. The pathogen causes wheat leaves to yellow\nand die, but it's not caused by wheat streak mosaic, head death or\nfreezing.\n'We're pretty sure it's a virus,' said wheat breeder Joe Martin, who\nworks at the Kansas State University research station at Hays. 'It\nshowed up early and, at first glance, we thought it was wheat streak\nmosaic. But it's not. It kills the oldest leaves of the plant and\nfinally kills the head.' Researchers don't know what the virus is,\nwhere it came from, or how it spreads.\nMartin said he's seen evidence of the virus in almost every field\nhe's checked in western Kansas, but it hasn't taken over the crop. He\nencouraged farmers to be on the lookout when checking their fields.\nDallas Seifers, a plant pathology professor at Fort Hays State\nUniversity, is trying to determine how the pathogen works, and what\nit might be.\n'It's possible that this is something that has been identified\nsomewhere else in the world, even something that has shown up in a\ndifferent crop, corn or rice or something,' Seifers said.\nSeifers, with the help of some virologists in Winnipeg, Canada, is\ntrying to identify the protein that causes the virus' symptoms. That\nwork is complicated by the fact that most affected plants found in\nthe field are already dead. Seifers is trying to grow his own supply\nof infected plants to study, but the effort hasn't been as successful\nas he hoped.\nOnce researchers identify the protein's genetic sequence, they can\ncompare it to known pathogens to find a match, or one that is in the\nsame family.\nSeifers said it's possible that the virus is showing up now because\nof recent unusual weather patterns, and that it wouldn't show up in a\nnormal year.\n'We're just happy that it is not in large enough numbers to have an\neconomic impact this year, and we hope it will be spotty if it shows\nup next year,' he said.\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[A 28-kD protein has been specifically associated with infected\nplants. AIMS scientists working in the long-term monitoring\nprogram say the disease they have documented is in a broad category\nknown as White Syndrome. Soon they hope to learn exactly what White\nSyndrome is.\nCathie Page, a deep ocean ecologist on the AIMS long term monitoring\nteam, says, 'It's more common on table corals. It starts at the base\nand works its way up. The disease breaks the coral tissue down,\neventually killing it.'\n'It doesn't fit the description of diseases found anywhere else in\nthe world, so it might be specific to the Pacific,' she says. In the\n3 years Page has been on the monitoring team, she has logged about\n450 dives spanning 48 reefs. She has seen White Syndrome kill at\nvarying rates.\n'It could kill a colony of 2 metres (6.5 feet) in diameter in 2 weeks\nbut in some other cases, it takes months to kill a large colony,' she\nsaid.\nThe first record of coral diseases came from reefs off Belize and\nFlorida in 1973. In 1993 coral diseases were noticed on the Great\nBarrier Reef. When the diseases worsened in the late 1990s, the\nlong-term monitoring team started documenting their activity. In\n1999 only 7 reefs were infected with White Syndrome; in 2002 33\nreefs were affected out of the 48 studied by the AIMS long-term\nmonitoring team.\nThe highest number of infected colonies within one reef was 101 in a\n1500-square-meter area. That was on Carter Reef, an outer shelf reef\nin the Cooktown/Lizard Island sector. The syndrome killed those\ncolonies infected and caused a decline in hard coral cover on this\nreef.\nAIMS scientists together with researchers from James Cook University\nwho are collaborating on the project have recorded the disease in\nnorthern waters during the winter months. Outer-shelf reefs near\nLizard Island off Cooktown in the northern Great Barrier Reef and the\nCapricorn Bunker reefs in the southern Great Barrier Reef are the\nworst affected areas.\nWhite Syndrome outbreaks are happening in pristine areas of the Great\nBarrier Reef, the AIMS teams says, on outer reefs untouched by\ncoastal development and tourism. This means the reef diseases are not\nlinked to pollution, as are other coral diseases around the world.\nCoral bleaching is also affecting the great reef, and scientists fear\nWhite Syndrome could be spreading more quickly in corals weakened by\nbleaching.\nCoral bleaching is the name given to an event in which coral expel\ntheir symbiotic algae due to extreme stress, such as unusually hot\nwater, according to AIMS bleaching expert Dr. Terry Done.\nThe bleached corals die if the stress is extreme or prolonged. With\nrising water temperatures over the tropical summers, coral bleaching\nevents are more widespread and happening more often, leaving little\ntime for coral to recover.\n'Bleached coral is not healthy and potentially more susceptible to\ndiseases,' said Page. 'We don't know what's causing this disease.\nIt's microscopic; it could be a range of things.'\nAIMS has sent samples of corals affected by White Syndrome away for\ntesting. When the results come back, AIMS will search for solutions\nthat might save the corals of the Great Barrier Reef.\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[The coral reef bleaching is a serious problem for the ocean life\nthat live in and around the reef, but the devastation of the reef has\nconsequences for the land mass that the reef protects as well. There\nare many theories, including the rise in ocean water temperatures as\nreflected by our warming climate, a potential effect of El Nino, and\neven contamination due to human waste. It may be a combination of\nthese that has allowed the problem to escalate, but whatever the\ncause, it is affecting the reefs on almost a worldwide basis. -\nMod.TG]", "summary": "A ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail, a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n Outer-shelf reefs near\nLizard Island off Cooktown in the northern Great Barrier Reef and the\nCapricorn Bunker reefs in the southern Great Barrier Reef are the\nworst affected areas. Frankel <Richard.Frankel@med.va.gov>\n\n\nHansen's disease is the preferred terminology in the USA.\n\nThe national figures have shown fewer cases in recent years. [CDC's]MMWR\nreported 93 cases in 2003 and 82 cases in 2004. The disease is not\nreportable in all states, so there may be a few more.\n\nIt is hard to understand why 7 to 10 days are needed to confirm the\ndiagnosis. While the disease is often misdiagnosed, once it is\nsuspected, a competent dermatopathologist should be able to confirm\nthe diagnosis.\n\nIsolation is generally not used for patients with Hansen's disease in\nthe USA. While there are differences of opinion with regard to the\ndegree of contagiousness, most people have natural immunity, and the\ninstitution of antimicrobial therapy quickly reduces the risk of\ntransmission.\n\n--\nRichard I. Frankel, MD, MPH\nVA Pacific Islands Health Care System\nProfessor Emeritus, University of Hawaii\nHonolulu, HI\n<Richard.Frankel@med.va.gov>\n\n[ProMED thanks Dr. Frankel for his comments.\n\nWhere the inmate spent his life from youth to incarceration is not\nstated. The Levis and Ernst chapter referenced below (1) reports\nthat in 2002, WHO reported over 600 000 new cases of leprosy, also\ncalled Hansen's disease (which as Dr. Frankel states is the preferred\nterminology), with the largest number of cases originating in South\nAsia (India, Bangladesh, Nepal and Myanmar). Africa and the Americas\neach reported about 40 000 new cases, with most of the Americas cases\nfrom Brazil.\n\nLevis and Ernst also note that _Mycobacterium leprae_ was the 1st\nbacterium to be associated with a disease. The Norwegian Armauer\nHansen discovered the organism in 1874 just prior to Koch's discovery\nof the the tubercle bacillus. The inability to cultivate _M. leprae_\non artificial media (which persists today) allowed Koch to be\ncredited with the discovery opening the germ theory of disease.\n\nIn the USA, _M. leprae_ is known to have been transmitted in several\nstates: Louisiana, Texas, Hawaii, and possibly California. 2 cases\nhave been reported, however, in residents of the eastern USA who had\nno obvious history of relevant travel or exposure (2).\n\n1. Levis WR, Ernst JD: Mycobacterium leprae (Leprosy, Hansen's\ndisease). In, Mandell, Douglas, and Bennett's Principles and Practice\nof Infectious Diseases, Mandell GL, Bennett JE, Dolin R (eds). 6th\ned., Elsevier Churchill Livingstone, Philadelhia, PA, 2005, pp\n2886-96.\n\n2. He\nmentioned botulism as one disease that might match the symptoms.\n\nTwo people were in critical condition and on life support, Mayor John\nSpencer said. But tests showed no\nairborne contamination or contagion, Spencer said. Cola said the victims'\nconditions deteriorated quickly.\n\nThe victims, whose names were not released, had eaten together in the\napartment less than a mile north of the New York city line.
