A sixth person was treated\nand released. The six went into respiratory arrest after eating dinner in a\nYonkers apartment. Others in the apartment who did not eat the meal did not\nbecome sick, the police said.\nBecause an ambulance worker developed a rash after lifting one of the\nvictims, the police initially thought the incident could have been a far\nmore serious outbreak or attack. The rash is now believed to have been\neither a coincidence or a result of contact with a victim's bodily fluids.\nUntil medical officials can pinpoint the cause of the illness, the\nauthorities are treating the case as a possible crime. 'We are looking at\nsubstances in the food,' said the Yonkers police commissioner, Charles A.\nCola. 'There are preservatives that can cause these symptoms. But at this\nlate date, we can say it wasn't cyanide.'\nThe police responded to a call at 6:17 Thursday night for what appeared to\nbe an incident of food poisoning in a modest four-story row house, not far\nfrom the city's downtown. But because of the severity of the symptoms and\nthe skin reaction of the medical technician, city officials went into full\ncrisis mode.\nThe Federal Bureau of Investigation, the Westchester County district\nattorney's office and a team of hazardous materials experts were all called\nin. The neighborhood surrounding the apartment building was closed off, as\nwas St. Joseph's emergency room. And the American Red Cross started to set\nup an emergency shelter at a nearby church.\n'We're dealing with so many unknowns in our society, as we're all painfully\naware of,' Mayor John D. Spencer said at a news conference. 'As a\ngovernment, as a city, we have to be prepared to be overly cautious when\ndealing with issues such as chemicals or strange occurrences, which this\nwas yesterday.'\nThe six victims \u0097 four men and two women of Egyptian heritage who range in\nage from 23 to 60 \u0097 apparently used some ingredients that were brought to\nthe United States from Egypt, Commissioner Cola said. 'Right now I'm\nleaning toward this being a non-crime, based on medical advice that it\ncould have happened naturally,' he said.\nThere was no move to recall any particular food item because a number of\ningredients were used in the dinner. 'We don't know what it is, so how do I\nsay, `It's the A.& P.'?' Commissioner Cola said.\nDr. Nicholas E. DeRobertis, director of emergency services at St. Joseph's\nMedical Center, said the list of substances that could provoke such a\nreaction was 'pretty extensive,' including certain antibiotics and food\npreservatives. The patients suffered from a condition he called\nmethemoglobinemia, which changes the red blood cells so that they cannot\ncarry oxygen to the body's tissues.\n'When that happens, people come in with severe respiratory distress, a\nbluish color and altered mental state,' Dr. DeRobertis said at the news\nconference.\nMr. Cola said the patients were immediately given an antidote for cyanide\npoisoning as a precaution.\nFoods from the meal were being tested at a federal Food and Drug\nAdministration laboratory in Queens, said Heather McGill, a spokeswoman for\nthe Westchester County Health Department. It was not known when the test\nresults would be made available, she said.\n[Byline: Lisa W. Foderaro]\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[2]\nDate: Date: Fri, 17 May 2002 16:14:11 -0700\nFrom: 'Carol H. Knott' <ctn43074@centurytel.net>\nSource: Newsday [edited]\nhttp://www.newsday.com/news/local/wire/ny-bc-ny--mysteriousillness0517may17.story?coll=ny%2Dap%2Dregional%2Dwire\n\nYONKERS, N.Y. -- Doctors blamed tainted food Friday for the sudden\nillnesses that set off a chemical-contamination scare in downtown\nYonkers. The police commissioner said he doubted there had been any foul\nplay. Two of the victims remained in critical condition a day after the\noutbreak of a rare blood-cell disease. Three were in stable condition and\none was released from the hospital.\n'I'm leaning toward non-crime based on medical advice,' said Commissioner\nCharles Cola. 'Nobody has told us this is something that somebody put in\nthe food.' He added, however, that police were still treating the victims'\napartment as a crime scene and that 'It would be presumptuous of me to rule\nout foul play.'\nMayor John Spencer said Yonkers was 'back to normalcy' after spinning into\nemergency mode Thursday night. The six victims had been taken to St.\nJoseph's Medical Center with severe breathing problems, a bluish pallor and\nan altered mental state. Some emergency workers reported picking up a rash\nas they treated the patients, adding to the concern.\nThe hospital was closed briefly and police, firefighters,\nhazardous-materials workers and even anti-terrorist agents streamed into\nthe area. The mayor mentioned the possibility of cyanide poisoning. A\ndecontamination shower was set up outside the victims' home. Air tests in\nthe building and at the hospital found no airborne contamination, however.\nWhen police learned that people in the apartment who had not eaten did not\nget sick, the investigation focused on the food. Cola said the victims,\nwho were identified only as being adults and of Egyptian heritage, were at\na dinner party featuring a dish with many ingredients, including a\nprocessed food that they had brought in from Egypt.\n'They became concerned about the taste of the food and quickly became ill,'\nhe said. He said the investigation was concentrating 'on the apartment and\nthe food itself and the way it was prepared,' rather than looking into\nwhether the victims had enemies who might have tampered with the food.\nDr. Nicholas DeRobertis, emergency director at St. Joseph's, said something\nthe victims ingested had changed their red blood cells into abnormal cells\nthat blocked the transfer of oxygen to tissue, a condition called\nmethemoglobinemia. It is unlike ordinary food poisoning, he said, in that\nit is a respiratory rather than gastrointestinal illness. He said he had\nseen it only once before, 15 or 20 years ago.\nThe doctor said the condition has more than 100 known causes, including\nunsafe levels of nitroglycerin; the antibiotics known as sulfonamides; or\nnaphthalene, which is used in mothballs. It is also used in some food\npreservatives, he said, but in that form would have to be ingested in 'very\nlarge quantities' to inflict the illness. He said tests that might show if\nthe food was tampered with could take weeks. The mayor said it was\npremature to try recalls or other warnings about tainted food because\n'there could be 100 different ways' that the toxin got into the food.\n[By Jim Fitzgerald]\n--\nCarol H. Knott\n<ctn43074@centurytel.net>\n\n[The earlier reports on this event suggested cyanide poisoning and then\nlater botulism. The present reports state that the clinical picture was\nconsistent with methemoglobinemia. Cyanide poisoning can present with a\nclinical picture similar to that seen with acquired methemoglobinemia. The\nearlier report on possible botulism is difficult to understand other than a\nclinical presentation of respiratory distress. A good review of\nmethemoglobinemia can be found at the Vanderbilt Medical College website:\n<http://www.mc.vanderbilt.edu/peds/pidl/hemeonc/index.htm>\nMethemoglobin is an abnormal hemoglobin that is not capable of carrying\noxygen or carbon dioxide. In adults and normal children the level of\nmethemoglobin is less than 1% of the total hemoglobin. Acquired\nmethemoglobinemia (presence of methemoglobin in the blood) results when the\nrate of formation of methemoglobin exceeds the rate of reduction after\nexposure to certain compounds. Nitrites and aniline derivatives are\nsubstances which most frequently produce methemoglobinemia. Because of its\nuse as a meat preservative and its similarity in appearance to table salt,\nsodium nitrite is frequently the cause of methemoglobinemia. Nitrites are\nalso present in many medicinal agents. Mosts reports of nitrate- induced\nmethemoglobinemia, however, are due to infants fed well water contaminated\nwith high levels of nitrates. Nitrate salts are converted by enteric\nbacteria to nitrites which are then rapidly absorbed from the\ngastrointestinal tract. Silver nitrate used on burns is also a common\nsource as bacteria infecting burns may similarly cause nitrite production.\nAniline and its derivitives are found in many household products such as\ninks, shoe polishes, paints and varnishes, and in some red and orange wax\ncrayons. Other drugs commonly associated with methemoglobinemia include\nphenacetin, sulfonamides, and pyridium. Benzocaine, a common ingredient of\ntopical anesthetics has also been known to cause marked cyanosis from\nmethemoglobinemia.\nSymptoms of methemoglobinemia include headaches, fatigue, coma, and death.\nHeadache, fatigue, tachycardia (fast heartrate), weakness and dizziness do\nnot appear until levels reach 30- 40%. At 50- 60% oxygenation of tissues\nbecomes truly inadequate resulting in dyspnea (shortness of breath),\nacidosis, arrhythmias (irregular heart rhythms), coma, and convulsions.\nDeath occurs with concentrations of about 70% and greater. Treatment\ninvolves general supportive care and removal of any offending toxins. The\ndrug of choice for treating severe methemoglobinemia is methylene\nblue. Severe cases may require exchange transfusion or the use of\nascorbic acid.\nMethemoglobinemia has been associated with ingestion of food products\ncontaining toxic levels of nitrites/nitrates or other substances. An\noutbreak in India (ref.1) was associated with ingestion of rice\ncontaminated with metanil yellow used for coloring the rice. Other\noutbreaks have been associated with the use of excessive amounts of sodium\nnitrate (saltpetre) in the preparation of sausages and other meat products\n(refs. 2,3).\nMore information on the etiology of the methemoglobinemia in this outbreak\nwould be appreciated.\n1: Sachdeva SM, Mani KV, Adaval SK, Jalpota YP, Rasela KC, Chadha\nDS. Acquired toxic methaemoglobinaemia. J Assoc Physicians India. 1992\nApr;40(4):239-40.\n2: Kennedy N, Smith CP, McWhinney P. Faulty sausage production causing\nmethaemoglobinaemia. They've dubbed it\n'black water', and have called local, state, and national government\nagencies to investigate.\nScientists who have heard of the phenomenon say they need answers too.'It's\nkilled a lot of the bottom because recently a lot of little bottom plants\nare coming to the surface dead and rotten out in the Gulf,' said Tim\nDaniels, 58, a Marathon Key fish-spotting pilot who has been flying over\nthe Gulf for more than 20 years. Experienced fishermen say they've often\nseen red tide but they've never seen anything like this 'it doesn't have a\nfoul smell, it isn't red tide and it isn't oil. They describe it as viscous\nand slimy water with what looks like spider webs in it.'\nFirst sighted in January, the mass of black-colored water reached from 20\nmiles north of Marathon Key halfway to Naples. It stretched west almost 20\nmiles into the Gulf of Mexico.\nThough somewhat smaller now than descriptions from January, the mass of\nwater is still quite large and is moving into the Florida Keys National\nMarine Sanctuary, a 2800 square-mile sanctuary adjacent to the Keys, which\nis the largest coral reef in the United States. It includes the productive\nwaters of Florida Bay, the Gulf of Mexico, and the Atlantic Ocean. Part of\nthe ecosystem is an extensive nursery, feeding, and breeding ground,\nsupporting a variety of marine species and a multimillion dollar fishing\nindustry bringing in almost 20 million pounds of seafood each year.\nBilly Causey, superintendent of the sanctuary, told the Naples Daily News\nrecently that there is real concern in the scientific community about the\noverall health of the Gulf. Causey said contributing to the problems\nafflicting the shallow body is global warming, extended periods when the\nGulf waters aren't cooling in the winter, and the growing impact of human\nactivity along coastlines. Those problems, beginning in the early 1980s,\ninclude more frequent and longer lasting coral bleaching events that by\n1990 were affecting stouter coral reefs closer to shore and more adapted to\nwide temperature swings.\n'There are places that are still beautiful but the shallow reefs would make\nyou cry,' said Causey, a Keys diver since the 1950s. Scientists with Mote\nMarine Laboratory based in Sarasota said they are aware of the black water\nphenomenon but have not yet been able to test water samples. Mote is\nwilling to send out testing kits to fishermen who might encounter the black\nwater zone but, in the absence of a kit, fishermen could put a sample in a\nclean bottle and keep it in a cool, dark place until they could get it to a\nlab.\nDaniels said he first noticed the black water when he went out in\nmid-January, ahead of kingfish season, to see what fishermen had in store\nfor 2002. When he was flying over water that was 50 feet deep and north of\nthe Keys, Daniels began to notice a change in the water color. When pilots\nfrom the air see boats move through a red tide zone, they often cut the\nreddish or brownish water to reveal green below. That doesn't occur in the\nblack water. 'This (dark) stuff goes all the way to the bottom,' Richardson\nsaid. Boats that have 4 to 5 feet of hull below the surface cut through 35\nto 40 feet of water and leave nothing but the same black water in their\nwakes. It's the same at depths of 15 feet, he said.\nAlong with the newly discovered black water and coral bleaching, there have\nbeen other problems with the Gulf having been documented for years. They\ninclude a New Jersey-sized dead zone coming off the Mississippi River\noutlet to the Gulf that consumes a larger area each summer. There are\nincidences of a contamination known as fibro papilloma [any information\nabout this condition? - Mod.SH] in green turtles that live in Florida Bay.\nThere are other problems in shrimp and an entire marine ecosystem appears\nto be sick.\n\u00ad\u00ad\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[The black water is a mystery requiring more water testing but apparently\ndefying life. Pollack <pollackmp@mindspring.com>\nSource: Reuters Online, 27 Oct 2000 [edited]\n\nStudy: Oregon River Water Causing Fish Deformities\n--------------------------------------------------\nPORTLAND, Oregon - Deformed fish found for years in a stretch of Oregon's\nWillamette River were damaged by something in the water, not by genetic\ndefects as had previously been believed, according to a new study\nreleased on Friday.\nScientists, who called their findings 'shocking,' said they were\nworking to determine the exact cause of the problem, and investigating\nwhether there were health risks associated with eating the deformed fish\nfound in a 30-mile section of the river.\n'It could be chemical, bacterial, parasites, high river temperature,\nlow oxygen levels, a variety of things,' said Steve Ellis, a scientist\nwith EVS Environment Consultants, the Seattle-based firm conducting the\nstudy.\n'We need to continue to study this and determine the cause and sources\nof the problem and then do something about it, which we will do,' said\nDick Pedersen, manager of the watershed management section of Oregon's\nDepartment of Environmental Quality.\nThe study was conducted near a stretch of the Willamette between Newberg\nand Oregon City, scientists said. There, 3500 rainbow trout eggs from a\nCalifornia trout farm were left above a river bed for 2 weeks until eyes\ncould be seen. They were then taken to a lab, reared to the fry stage,\nand studied against trout raised only in a laboratory.\nOf 372 trout sampled, 34 percent exposed to Willamette River water for 2\nweeks had deformities compared with 9 percent of the fish raised in the\nlaboratory, the study found.\n'The types of skeletal deformities we saw are the same type as with\nother fish' having come out of the Willamette, EVS's Ellis said. In\naddition, prior studies have shown random samples of fish from the this\npart of the river have had deformity rates above 70 percent, scientists\nsaid.\nAbout 70 percent of Oregon's population lives within 20 miles of the\nWillamette River, making it an important symbol for Oregonians, Allen\nsaid, adding, 'This is a slap upside the head for Oregonians.'\nThe river, which winds through the state's most populated areas, is also\nplanned as a source of drinking water for the town of Wilsonville in\n2002.\nEllis's firm is working on a study of the health risks of eating fish\ncaught on this stretch of the Willamette.\n'We are still dumping a lot of chemicals in this part of the river,'\nAllen said. 'A lot of people think this is stuff that happened 40 years\nago. Dumping [is] a current problem.'\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[If they knew who was dumping chemicals, then something could perhaps\nmore easily be done. Scientists, who called their findings 'shocking,' said they were\nworking to determine the exact cause of the problem, and investigating\nwhether there were health risks associated with eating the deformed fish\nfound in a 30-mile section of the river. Pollack <pollackmp@mindspring.com>\nSource: AP Online, 31 Aug 2000 12:38 PM EDT [edited]\n\nUkraine Region Declared Disaster\n---------------------------------\nKIEV, Ukraine (AP) -- President Leonid Kuchma on Thursday declared 4\nsouthern Ukrainian villages an ecological disaster zone, following an\noutbreak of a mysterious illness some have blamed on leaks of Soviet-era\nrocket fuel.\nAbout 400 residents of the villages near Mykolaiv, 320 miles south of the\ncapital Kiev, have been reported sick since 4 Jul 2000, but only a few new\ncases were registered this week, Health Minister Vitaliy Moskalenko said.\nHealth officials were checking nearly 6 000 residents of nearby villages\nfor signs of the illness, a chemical poisoning [it is not established on\nthe basis of this and the next report that the illness is due to chemical\nexposure -Man. Ed. DS] that causes skin rashes and affects the liver and\npancreas, he told a state investigative commission.\nHigh concentrations of nitrates have been found in 57 percent of drinking\nwater supplied through a pipe system, 98 percent of water from wells and\nevery tenth food product checked, Moskalenko said in comments cited by the\nInterfax news agency.\nOfficials said Ukraine would appeal to the World Health Organization and\nforeign governments to help it deal with the emergency. The government,\nmeanwhile, appeared split on what caused the illness, with some officials\nblaming rocket fuel and others denying the possibility. In the region is a\nbase holding solid-fuel SS-24 nuclear missiles, which are to be dismantled\nin 2001. It once housed other Soviet missiles powered by liquid fuel.\nHealth experts have said the area's soil and water contained substances\nthat are usually produced by decomposing rocket fuel, but Kuchma's\nspokesman Oleksandr Martynenko insisted on Wednesday that rocket fuel could\nnot be blamed. Instead, he suggested that the illness could have resulted\nfrom high amounts of nitrates in the soil. But the head of the government\ncommission, deputy premier Mykola Zhulynskyi, said missile silos in the\narea had remained open after liquid-fuel rockets were dismantled there in\nthe late 1970s. Fuel spills could have occurred during the missiles'\ndismantling, he said. Ukraine inherited 46 SS-24 and 130 SS-19 nuclear\nmissiles following the 1991 Soviet collapse. Kiev has since surrendered all\nits nuclear warheads to Russia and eliminated the last SS-19 missile in\n1999. Most of the SS-24s along with missile silos remain to be destroyed\nunder a disarmament plan running through 2001.\n[Byline: Sergei Shargorodsky]\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n***\n[2]\nDate: 31 Aug 2000 20:38:33 -0400\nFrom: Marjorie P. Such patients have been visiting the out-door\npatient departments (OPDs) and casualty departments of government hospitals\nin the city almost daily. However, most of the cases are being reported at\nprivate clinics of general physicians every day.\nAttributing the increase in the cases of gastroenteritis to the prevailing\nunhygienic conditions, a polluted environment and impure water, doctors\nsaid such patients complained of pain in the abdomen, vomited and suffered\nfrom diarrhoea. They advised people that as soon as they come across a\nperson having the above-mentioned symptoms, they must take him or her to a\nnearby hospital or clinic because excessive vomiting and diarrhoea lead to\ndehydration.\nConfirming that the cases of gastroenteritis which had shot up during May\nhave not yet subsided, doctors said as the cases of gastroenteritis would\ncontinue to increase till August, people must drink a sufficient quantity\nof boiled water, besides avoiding stale food and fruits. According to an\nRMO [Regional Medical Officer?] at the Jinnah Postgraduate Medical Centre\n(JPMC), the number of patients suffering from gastroenteritis at the\nhospital's casualty department in 24 hours had increased to about 30 as\nagainst 15 to 20 such cases during normal days. A doctor at the Civil\nHospital's casualty department also confirmed that the number of\ngastroenteritis patients was on the rise as from 10 to 15 such patients\nvisited the hospital's emergency unit daily. However, these figures did not\ninclude those who visit the hospital's OPDs daily, he said.\n--\nProMED-mail\ne-mail: promed@usa.healthnet.org\n......................................es\n--\n*##########################################################*\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. (02)\n [1]\n Applied Physics Lab, Air Defense Systems Dept.\n promed@promedmail.org\n **\n \n \n", "reports": [{"diseases": ["unknown", "other", "malaria"], "syndromes": ["meningitis"], "event_date": ["2021-08-24 00:00:00", "1997-03-24 00:00:00", "1997-12-24 00:00:00", "1997-12-18 00:00:00", "2021-03-26 00:00:00"], "locations": [{"location": "Yapsie", "country": "unknown"}, {"location": "Papua New Guinea", "country": "Papua New Guinea"}, {"location": "West Sepik", "country": "Papua New Guinea"}]}]}, {"archive_id": "2192375", "headline": "PRO/AH/EDR> Pneumonia, snake, unknown etiology (02)", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=2192375", "date": "1997-12-12 23:50:00", "main_text": "PNEUMONIA, SNAKE, UNKNOWN ETIOLOGY (02)\n***************************************\nA ProMED-mail post", "summary": "", "reports": [{"diseases": ["unknown"], "syndromes": [], "event_date": [], "locations": []}]}, {"archive_id": "2192458", "headline": "PRO/EDR> Encephalopathy, etiology unknown - Dem. Rep. of Congo", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=2192458", "date": "1997-12-31 23:50:00", "main_text": "ENCEPHALOPATHY, ETIOLOGY UNKNOWN - DEMOCRATIC REPUBLIC OF CONGO\n***************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nDate: Tue, 30 Dec 97 18:38:28 UTC\nFrom: Evangelical Hospital, Democratic Republic of Congo\n<vanga@zre.healthnet.org> or <clemmer@maf.org>\n\nThis report comes from Vanga Hospital in the Democratic Republic of Congo\n(former Zaire) where two cases of encephalopathy of undetermined etiology\npresented this week at this 400 bed mission hospital located in the\ninterior of the Republic of Congo 80 kilometers upriver from Kikwit .\nTwo school age children from different villages in the Vanga Health\nDistrict (5-7 kilometers apart) presented to the reference hospital with\nsymptoms consistent with a viral gastroenteritis. Both evolved rapidly\ninto a coma. The first child died within 48 hours, the second is at present\nstill comatose. The children attended different schools and secured water\nand food from different sources. No family members to date have contracted\nthis illness.\nThe cases are as follows:\nPatient 1 (hospitalized 12/18/97)\nThe first patient, an eight year old boy from the village Songo, 6 km from\nVanga fell ill on a Friday after school and died 2 days later on Sunday\nevening. The child in otherwise good health had been seen at Vanga\nHospital five days earlier for a sprained ankle sustained while playing\nsoccer. He was given aspirin and an ace bandage. On the first day of his\nillness he experienced colicky abdominal pain with persistent vomiting. He\nwas treated locally with chloramphenicol and an anti-spasmodic (papaverine)\nThe following day he was referred to the Vanga Hospital where clinical\nexam by a physician suggested viral gastroenteritis in an otherwise healthy\nchild. He was afebrile, a malaria smear was negative and white blood count\nwas 12,150mm3. The child was hospitalized for observation. Chloramphenical\nand an antispasmodic were continued.\nEarly the following morning the night nurse found the boy in a deep coma\nand signaled the physician on call. The child was febrile (38 C) with\ntachycardia (120) and tachypnea (48). He was unresponsive to all stimuli.\nPupils were dilated and [un?]responsive to light. Diffuse hypotonia and\nhyporeflexia were noted. Babinski test was negative. Lungs were clear and\nheart sounds normal. Presenting signs have\nbeen either death with hemorrhage from the oral cavity or 24-48 hrs of\nrales/oral cavity mucus followed by death, whether antibiotics have been\nstarted or not.\nThus far, gross pathology have been severe hemorrhagic, purulent to\ndiphtheritic pneumonia and histopathology has seemed more bacterial than\nviral, although viral cultures are still pending. One suggests a real world cause, one\nsuggests sorcery. As attempted sorcery is no less real than attempted\ndiagnosis, the reports are combined. - Mod.CHC]\n[1]\n[Digested] report by Dr Stephen Flew, Senior Medical Office, Ok Tedi Mining\nLtd, (written for Papua New Guinea Department of Health); Re: Outbreak of\nunknown disease /excess deaths, Sandaun Province\n[Investigation] indicated the [people] at Tapsie village were mostly\naffected by the usual skin afflictions common to the area such as grille\n(tinea imbicata), tropical ulcers, yaws, etc. as well as malaria,\nfilariasis, tropical splenomegaly and pneumonia. However there did not\nappear to be any excess of morbidity or mortality at this time, nor during\nthe drought. [The investigators] were told that the most affected areas were\nUrapmin and Ibikmen but that people had fled their usual dwellings due to\nfear of sorcery and were living in bush houses. They were strongly advised\nnot to go to these areas on foot by the people at Yapsie, because of the\ndangers of sorcery. The team were willing to go into Urapmin by chopper so\nwe flew them [there], accompanied by a local guide. The main village of\nUrapmin appeared deserted so we proceeded up the Aki river to an isolated\nhamlet and managed to land the chopper on a tiny beach in a nearby creek.\nThere seemed to be about 20-30 people living here, many covered in 'grille'\nand with swollen bellies but seemed to be saying they were all OK, as far as\nI could make out above the noise of the chopper. The terrain here is very\nbroken and mountainous and I believe these people must be in a chronic state\nof poor health, with no ready access to any form of health care. There did\nnot appear to have been any deaths there but we left a team behind to\ninvestigate further.\nThe other team (from the Health Dept. in Vanimo) had gone to Ibikmin\nvillage. When we arrived they had already left; apparently there were no\nproblems there either.\nWe proceeded to another isolated hamlet on a heavily forested ridge, known\nas Finyaksolmin. The second team had only just arrived the night before and\nhad had no chance to check the local population yet. They were told there\nhad been no deaths here but 2 people had died at nearby Firayabamin, one\nolder woman of COAD [?] and a young man of malaria (?).\nBack at Yapsie [the health worker] who had been left in charge for the last\nfew months reported that health-wise things [were bad but] hadn't really got\nany worse during the drought, with a high prevalence of childhood\nmalnutrition (30-50%) and many patients with chronic anaemia and\nhepatosplenomegaly (secondary to filariasis and malaria). There is a high\nproportion of refugees now residing amongst the locals at Yapsie who have\n[come] from over the border with Irian Jaya (just 10 kms away). The\npresence of the refugees in an already marginally productive environment\nexacerbates the malnutrition problem, and malnutrition is accepted as the\nnorm for growing children. No doubt the maternal, infant and childhood\nmortality rates must be amongst the highest in PNG, even under normal\nclimatological conditions. Even in October Yapsie appeared fairly green and\nnot much affected by drought. Now the Sepik river is in flood and there is\nlittle evidence of drought except for the extensive bushfires in the high\ncountry between here and Tabubil.\nA review of the Health Centre monthly reports at Yapsie indicates there was\nnot much change in outpatient illness rates for the common conditions of\ncough, pneumonia, other respiratory disease, diarrhoea, malaria, anaemia,\nyaws and other skin diseases during October-November (total of 1200\nattendances each month). During the first 3 weeks of December there appears\nto have been an increase in malaria, 'flu, diarrhoea and skin diseases (the\nlatter esp. from Munbil, ?some ulcers requiring skin grafts). However there\nhas been no increase in deaths recorded at Yapsie and the [administrator]\nfrom Fiak was also surprised to hear of the 10 deaths which were reported\nfrom his area, none of which he was aware of.\nIt would appear that the lay reporting of 19 deaths and 24-30 people\ncritically ill or comatose in the Yapsie and Fiak subdistricts of Telefomin\nhas been grossly exaggerated. The reporting of these deaths may have come\nabout due to the rumours of sorcery and the confusion arising from the\nabandonment of villages in the area. [He goes on to suggest that additional\nresources be made available to these isolated communities so that the\nincidence of filariasis, malaria, and other vector-borne diseases could be\nreduced.]\n\nDr. Stephen Flew, SMO\nOk Tedi Mining Ltd\nFlew.Stephen.S@bhp.com.au\n--\nDr J A Ballard, Visiting Fellow\nGraduate School, Australian National University, Canberra ACT 0200, Australia\nTel +61 2 6249 5487 Fax +61 2 6249 4829\nGraduate School web page http://online.anu.edu.au/academia/graduate/\ne-mail: john.ballard@anu.edu.au\n\n[2]\nDate: Wed, 24 Dec 1997 17:11:46 +0700 (JAVT)\nFrom: zulfian <ZULFIAN@JAYAPURA.WASANTARA.NET.ID>\nWe thank you for the attention and consideration on what happen in Irian\nJaya, especially in the highland of Jayawijaya.\nThe El Nino has affected the area to cause the drought since April 1997. It\nseems that the situation has incerased the temperature in the highland. Our\nconsideration is in the area above 1,700 m (5,000 feet) from sea level,\nwhich [has seen] several changes on the ecosystem.\nWe have clinically and laboratory confirmed that cerebral malaria has been\nfound in that area (Lolat, Weawen, and Kabianggema, these three villages are\nnot in the border of Papua New Guinea). Malaria are common in Irian Jaya;\nhowever, it was amazing because the disease had never been found [at that\naltitude]. A recent investigation by a team of entomologists,\nepidemiologists, and clinical laboratorians found that the _Anopheles\npunctulatus_ [?] has climbed up to higher altitude.\nBlood smear examination from 52 [people in the?] high prevalence area had\nalso confirmed that plasmodium infections were responsible for the\nmysterious disease. The parasite rate had been found 31.9% - 98.21% among\nthe suffering patients.\nThese villages listed below are endemic [for] malaria and are on the border\nof Papua New Guinea :\n\nVillage Parasite rate\nPepera 98.21%\nBulangkop 81.71%\nMimin 54.17%\nKabiding 31.90%\nOknagul 70.00%\nCurrently, the rate has decreased to 2% after a radical mass treatment with\nchloroquine.\nAn investigation is being conducted at village Okyop (a village close to\nYapsie of Papua New Guinea), since it was reported that same problem arise\nthere. We hope that the laboratory result (blood smear) can be confirmed\nwithin a week.\n--\nZulfian Muslim, MD\nHead, District Health Office\nDistrict of Jayawijaya\nIrian Jaya, Indonesia\n[So, we have a situation in which many serious infectious diseases are\nendemic and the current hypotheses are (1) there is no excess morbidity or\nmortality but (2) primitive beliefs are driving rumors of such illnesses and\ndeaths and (3) there is cerebral malaria in the area but that it is being\ntreated properly and successfully. We likely will not get to a diagnostic\nresolution of this situation. - Mod.CHC]\n...............................chc/es\n--\n*##########################################################*\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. province\ntoday to investigate the reported deaths of 16 people and attend to\ndozens of other villagers hit by an unknown epidemic.\nPeter Tavun, the provincial disaster and emergency services coordinator,\nsaid from Vanimo yesterday that the deaths had occurred in the Urapmin,\nSiarimin and Niyol villages in the Yapsie area of Telefomin district.\nMr Tavun said his office had received reports of the mystery disease\nfrom various sources but the headmaster of the Yapsie school on Saturday\nconfirmed the death of 16 people while 32 others were seriously ill.\n'Earlier, other reports areas\nreportedly hit by the unknown epidemic...\nThe Urapmin, Siarimin and Niyol villages have a total population of\nabout 1,000 people, according to available provincial data.\n\n17 December issue\n-----------------\nMystery disease claims 10 more\nBy ALPHONSE BARIASI\nLAE: The Catholic Church diocese of Vanimo yesterday reported another 10\ndeaths from the as yet unknown epidemic that 10\no'clock this morning to assess the situation. The team will be in\nYapsie conducting a field assessment. If there is any worsening of the\nepidemic the team will be stationed there for another two to three\nweeks, he said. The Yapsie area is accessible only by air and the medical team flying in\ntoday will have to walk for at least three days into the areas\nreportedly hit by the unknown epidemic...\n \nProMED-mail\ne-mail: promed@usa.healthnet.org\n A medical team will be sent to the Yapsie area of Sandaun province\ntoday to investigate the reported deaths of 16 people and attend to\ndozens of other villagers hit by an unknown epidemic. \n\nYesterday's figure would mean there had been altogether 26 deaths and\nmany others falling unconscious since the epidemic hit the remote\nvillages of the Telefomin district... Mr Tavun said his office had received reports of the mystery disease\nfrom various sources but the headmaster of the Yapsie school on Saturday\nconfirmed the death of 16 people while 32 others were seriously ill. Peter Tavun, the provincial disaster and emergency services coordinator,\nsaid from Vanimo yesterday that the deaths had occurred in the Urapmin,\nSiarimin and Niyol villages in the Yapsie area of Telefomin district. West Sepik administrator Jerry Poivi, who arrived in Vanimo from Port\nMoresby yesterday, said a medical team will be flown to Yapsie at 10\no'clock this morning to assess the situation. If there is any worsening of the\nepidemic the team will be stationed there for another two to three\nweeks, he said. Since September 15, hunters\nobserved at least seven animals suffering from a progressive palsy\naffecting first the posterior limbs and leading to death in about a week.\nAutopsies performed until now failed to reveal any etiology but a viral\nencephalitis is suspected by veterinarians who are still working on this\nproblem.\nThe question has been asked of a possible transmission to humans (it is the\nhunting season) or domestic animals (cattle might be in contact with\naffected wild animals). Does somebody out there have an idea for the\netiology, or any suggestion about public health measures that should be\nundertaken?\n[Any information would be appreciated.
